| Weft cross-Proc Burrow-share (the I-37 dataplane substrate) | `kernel/burrow.c` (NEW `burrow_share_into(dst, v, vaddr, prot)` -- map an existing Burrow into a SECOND Proc + take the 2nd #847 ref under `dst->vma_lock`; the existing `burrow_map` is already Proc-agnostic + #847-SMP-safe, so the new work is the cross-Proc dual-refcount PROOF + the thin helper), `kernel/syscall.c` (the Weft-6 EL0 delivery: `sys_weft_share_handler` [netd registers a Burrow as a flow's ring] + `sys_weft_map_handler` [the guest maps the flow's ring -> VA], keyed on the `/net` data fid), `kernel/include/thylacine/syscall.h` (`SYS_WEFT_SHARE = 81` / `SYS_WEFT_MAP = 82` + ABI; 80 reserved for `SYS_FD_DEVCLASS`), the netd + `/net` data-fid grant path | Weft arc (`docs/NET-THROUGHPUT.md` section 6; the committed throughput NOVEL, I-37). **The tree's FIRST cross-Proc shared page -- prosecute hard.** Realizes **I-37** (capability network dataplane integrity); **spec-first RE-ENABLED** (`specs/weft.tla`, the 5th instance of point (a) -- LANDED model-first at Weft-1). Delivery = **grant-is-the-share** (user-voted 2026-06-20; the Plan 9 mmap-the-server-file + Fuchsia IOBuffer RFC-0218 + seL4-coordinator convergent answer): opening the flow's `/net/<proto>/N/data` fid maps the per-flow shared Burrow into the guest -- NO Burrow handle ever crosses Procs (the kernel maps both sides; the #847 refs are kernel-internal; the capability IS holding the namespace-gated flow fid, I-1/I-28), so there is no free-floating dup-able Burrow handle to leak / retain past the flow / mis-target. *Capability delegation* (a Burrow handle crosses netd->guest, guest `SYS_BURROW_ATTACH`es it -- opens the deferred I-4 path + a dup-able cross-Proc handle to police) + an *explicit decoupled `SYS_FLOW_SHARE`/`MAP` pair* were rejected. Prosecute: the **#847 dual-refcount SMP-safety across two Procs concurrently mapping/unmapping one Burrow** (the load-bearing new property -- no Burrow has ever been reachable from two Procs; no UAF / double-free / leak; free iff BOTH refs drop -- `weft.tla::ShareBoundedByFlow`); the share is **bounded by the flow + fully dropped on teardown** (no stale mapping past the data-fid clunk -- `NoStaleShareAccess`, the allowance.tla RevokedFullyCleared analog); **W^X** on the shared mapping (RW-only, like SYS_BURROW_ATTACH); the **per-flow keying** (one ring per connection N, NOT per SrvConn -- joey mounts `/net` over ONE shared kernel dev9p session, so a per-flow share cannot key on the SrvConn); netd owns the NIC (I-5); the share reaches ONLY a Proc holding the flow fid (I-1/I-28). **Weft-2** lands the substrate (`burrow_share_into` + the cross-Proc dual-refcount proof + a kernel unit test; NO EL0 ABI -- the EL0 surface is flow-keyed, so it lands with the `/net` binding); **Weft-6** lands the EL0 delivery -- **keying fork resolved to Option B (lazy fid-keyed, user-voted 2026-06-20; NET-THROUGHPUT 6.1, superseding the earlier eager "data-fid auto-map" sketch):** a new `Tweft(F)->Rweft(share_id, geom)` 9P op (`P9_TWEFT=142`/`P9_RWEFT=143` since the #371 renumber -- born 134/135, latently colliding with Stratum `Tfadvise`/`Tpin`; the registry is `docs/9P-EXTENSIONS.md`; the **#845 Tflush precedent** -- a kernel-client-issued op netd handles) + `SYS_WEFT_SHARE(ring_va, ring_size)->share_id` (netd-side 81: alloc+init the per-flow ring in netd's AS, pin the backing ANON Burrow [I-30, **RW-only W^X**], mint a kernel-scoped `share_id`) + `SYS_WEFT_MAP(data_fd, hint_va)->ring_va` (guest-side 82: resolve data_fd->(client,F) via `dev9p_client_fid`, issue `Tweft(F)` on the FIRST zero-copy use, join the `Rweft` `share_id`->the pinned Burrow, `burrow_share_into` it into the guest, bind in `dev9p_priv`, idempotent). **LAZY** (only a zero-copy flow issues `Tweft`; small/control writes stay on the byte-copy ring -- the section-4.8 hybrid) + **fid-keyed** (the `share_id` is kernel-internal netd->kernel, NEVER handed to the guest -> unforgeable; honored only when it arrives on the kernel's own `Tweft` to that netd -- the RDMA-rkey shape). Teardown: the data-fid clunk (`dev9p_close`) drops BOTH #847 refs -> the ring freed (I-7; `ShareBoundedByFlow`/`NoStaleShareAccess`). Weft-3/4/5 go LIVE here (the desc ring on large Twrite/Tread + the readiness park/wake Rendez + the F_NOTIF holders driven by real netd/NIC/ACK events) + the native `libthyla_rs::net` push/pop/wait API. Split **6a** (kernel ABI: the 2 syscalls + `Tweft`/`Rweft` + the `dev9p_priv` binding + the `share_id` correlation + teardown + kernel tests) / **6b** (netd wiring) / **6c** (native API + in-guest E2E). The new `Tweft`/`share_id` correlation (consumed-exactly-once + no cross-flow mis-binding + netd-pin GC if the guest dies pre-map) is prose + **Weft-7**-audit validated (the spec stays unchanged -- setup plumbing abstracted as `Init`; extend it FIRST if 6a surfaces real subtlety). **Weft-7** the focused buffer-lifetime-UAF audit + the SMP gate + the benchmark. **`weft.tla` UNCHANGED** by the delivery choice (grant-is-the-share *realizes* the model's Init [the share mapped into both via the dual ref -- delivery-agnostic by construction]; the cross-Proc dual-refcount is burrow.tla's #847 domain; flow-containment is I-28's -- no new invariant-bearing mechanism, so the model written model-first at Weft-1 stands; spec-first satisfied). Prose validation in `docs/NET-THROUGHPUT.md` section 6 + ARCH section 25.4 + this row + the Weft-2 substrate test + the Weft-7 focused audit + the SMP gate. **Weft-6b-2 (the data-drive wire mechanism, user-voted 2026-06-20, NET-THROUGHPUT 6.2) ADDS the audit-bearing `Tweftio`/`Rweftio` op (`P9_TWEFTIO=144`/`P9_RWEFTIO=145` since #371; `kernel/9p_wire.c` + `p9_client_weftio` + the session arm) + the kernel WRITE FAST-PATH on the hot syscall (`kernel/syscall.c::sys_write_handler` -> `sys_write_weft_fastpath` -> `kernel/dev9p.c::dev9p_weft_try_write`, gated `len >= WEFT_HYBRID_THRESHOLD`) + the binding ring view (`kernel/weft.c::weft_binding_alloc` computes `weft_ring_view` at `SYS_WEFT_MAP`; `weft_binding_validate_write` = the I-30 validator-once over the trusted syscall-arg descriptor) + netd's in-place reader (`usr/netd/src/server.rs::h_weftio` reads the ring + `data_send`; TX-only at v1.0, RX = 6b-3). The synchronous buf-in-ring path bypasses the `SYS_RW_MAX` scratch (moves up to `payload_size`); the batched `weft_ring_drain` path is Weft-6c. As-built `docs/reference/125-weft.md` "The data drive"; the focused buffer-lifetime + Tweftio-correlation audit stays Weft-7.** **Weft-6b-3a (the symmetric RX direction) ADDS the read fast-path twin: `weft_binding_validate_write` -> `weft_binding_validate_rw` (direction-agnostic -- a Tweftio READ destination and a WRITE source both name a `[off,off+len)` payload window, so one validator serves both; the kernel test is `weft.binding_validate_rw`); `kernel/dev9p.c::dev9p_weft_try_read` + `kernel/syscall.c::sys_read_weft_fastpath` (gated `len >= WEFT_HYBRID_THRESHOLD`, before the SYS_RW_MAX clamp) issue `p9_client_weftio(READ)` -- and do NO `uaccess_store` (netd writes the recv'd bytes DIRECTLY into the guest's shared ring -> the true zero-copy property). netd's `h_weftio` gains the `WEFT_DIR_READ` arm: recv IN PLACE into the ring (`weft_recv_into_ring` -> `data_recv_outcome` over the in-place `&mut` slice); an empty-but-open socket DEFERS (park a `PendingWeftRead` + `Disp::Deferred`; `poll_weftio` delivers the held `Rweftio` when bytes arrive, or 0 on EOF) -- the net-6a-1 byte-copy `h_read`/`poll_data` twin, so a weft `recv()` BLOCKS instead of spuriously returning 0 (a 0 = EOF). Prosecute: the **I-9 no-lost-wake on the defer** (netd single-threaded -> `net.poll` runs before `poll_weftio` -> no readiness edge lost between the empty-observe and the park; register-then-observe like `poll_data`); the **4 cancel sites COMPLETE** (`PendingWeftRead` mirrors `pending_reads` at teardown/`fid_clunk`/`Tversion`/`Tflush` -- a missed cancel strands a held `Rweftio` tag, the net-4d F1 class); the **recv-into-ring memory safety** (`weft_recv_into_ring` re-resolves `weft_flow(n)` + re-bounds defensively, so a slot freed/re-minted mid-defer yields Eof, never an OOB write -- the net-3d slot-reuse discipline); the **blocking lifetime** (`p9_client_weftio` blocks on the held tag, death-interruptible, no per-op deadline, #841; session death completes it `-P9_E_IO`); pouch non-interaction (a pouch read buffer is never in a weft ring -> always byte-copy; weft RX is native-client-only). `weft.tla` UNCHANGED (the symmetric read direction of the modeled `Consume`; the 4 buggy cfgs re-ran green). Proven by `net-echo`'s `weft_rx_e2e` (`net-echo: weft-6b RX E2E PASS` -- the server sends, the client weft-reads INTO the ring over the loopback, exercising the FULL park/deliver defer; bytes verified in the client's own ring mapping). 961/961 + boot OK + 0 EXT; the live readiness park/wake (6b-3b) + the F_NOTIF posting (6b-3c) remain. As-built `docs/reference/125-weft.md` "The data drive" (the RX arm).** **Weft-6c-1 (the Loom data drive) ADDS the native-async zero-copy path over Loom -- NO new ABI (composes existing Loom+Weft, NET-THROUGHPUT 6): `kernel/loom.c::loom_submit_payload` detects a weft-bound `/net` data fid whose registered buffer is the flow's WHOLE shared ring (`buf == wb->burrow && buf_reg_len == wb->ring_size`; `dev9p_priv->weft` read `__atomic`-acquire) and routes the async LOOM_OP_READ/WRITE to `loom_build_weftio` (Tweftio off/len/dir) instead of `loom_build_read/write`; the slice validates via the REUSED `weft_binding_validate_rw(wb->guest_va + buf_off)` (whole-ring registration makes buf_off ring-base-relative; the guest_va cancels in the validator); `loom_payload_result`'s `op->weft` branch copies NOTHING (result = the Rweftio count -- the bytes moved in place). A non-ring buffer falls to the byte path (the section-4.8 hybrid); an in-ring OOB slice is `-EINVAL`. **The honest F_NOTIF realization**: a weft WRITE is a zero-copy send, but at v1.0 netd's h_weftio COPIES, so it is the io_uring SEND_ZC COPIED path -- a SINGLE terminal CQE (no LOOM_CQE_MORE), NO `loom_async_op.notif` field, no deferral; the deferred two-CQE (MORE then LOOM_CQE_F_NOTIF on the last {netd,NIC,ACK} holder clear) is the v1.x true-zero-copy seam (needs a netd-holds-the-page TX path + a netd->kernel holder-clear channel, neither at v1.0; the consumer reads LOOM_CQE_MORE to decide whether to wait -> forward-compatible). Prosecute (Weft-7/6c-3): the weft-binding read lifetime (`sp` pinned via spoor_ref -> the binding cannot be freed under the routing read [`dev9p_close`->`weft_binding_release` runs only at the last Spoor ref]; the `__atomic`-acquire matches the sync `dev9p_weft_try_rw` path); the whole-ring contract soundness (a whole-ring-size registration MUST start at Burrow offset 0 to fit one VMA, so buf_off is Burrow-relative even across a second mapping); I-30 (the offset is computed from the SQE snapshot + the kernel-private `wb->view`, never re-read from the shared ring); the buffer pin (#847, dropped at reap). `weft.tla` + `loom.tla` UNCHANGED (the copied case = `weft_notif_arm_copied` -> not-in-flight; the READ/WRITE drive = the symmetric `Consume`; all buggy cfgs re-ran green). Tests: `9p_client.loom_weft_{read,write,hybrid_fallback,oob_rejected}_e2e`. 965/965 + boot OK + 0 EXT at the 6c-1 landing; the native `libthyla_rs::net` API + the in-guest E2E are 6c-2, the focused buffer-lifetime audit + SMP gate are Weft-7 (6c-3). As-built `docs/reference/125-weft.md` "The Loom data drive".** **Weft-6c-2 (the native push/pop/wait API + the readiness edge) ADDS -- PURE USERSPACE, the kernel BYTE-UNCHANGED (a weft flow is just a Loom ring whose registered buffer is a `SYS_WEFT_MAP`'d region, which the 6c-1 kernel already detects): `usr/lib/libthyla-rs/src/net.rs::WeftFlow` (the Demikernel-shaped `push`/`pop`/`wait` over Loom -- `open(&TcpStream)` does `SYS_WEFT_MAP` + `read_ring_geom` + `Ring::setup` + register `(data fd, whole ring)`; `push(len)`/`pop(max)` stage a `LOOM_OP_WRITE`/`READ` SQE [`buf_off = payload_off`], `wait` does the io_uring submit-and-wait + parks on the **Loom CQ wait** [NET-THROUGHPUT 6: the park IS the CQ wait, no separate weft Rendez]; `tx_buf`/`rx_buf` for true zero-copy fill/read, `send`/`recv` convenience) + `usr/lib/libthyla-rs/src/weft.rs` (`read_ring_geom` [the geometry-mirror inverse: `ring_size = payload_off+payload_size`, the whole-Burrow size the routing requires] + the readiness-drive `ready_signal`/`ready_observe` -- the userspace mirror of the kernel `weft_ready_signal`/`weft_ready_observe`, the `weft_readiness.tla` store-buffer register-then-observe reproduced for the cross-Proc seq-cst story) + `usr/netd/src/server.rs::weft_recv_into_ring` (the `WEFT_READY_RX` edge on each real recv-into-ring -- the section-6 syscall-free busy-poll; netd ignores the wake-needed return since the client parks on the Loom CQE, not a weft Rendez -- the direct-park leg stays validated-not-wired, v1.x). **Single-in-flight** (the one payload region -> push XOR pop at a time; a 2nd before its `wait` -> `WouldBlock`); `WeftFlow` is `!Send`+`!Sync` (the raw `ring_va`) so it cannot race across threads; the borrow checker keeps `tx_buf`/`rx_buf` from outliving a submit. NO new ABI, NO new invariant, NO new spec module (composes Loom+Weft; the kernel byte-unchanged). Prosecute (Weft-7/6c-3): the single-in-flight buffer-lifetime contract (no in-flight ring mutation), the readiness cross-Proc seq-cst (the mirror reproduces the modeled orderings), the `register_buffers` whole-ring contract (`buf_reg_len == wb->ring_size`). v1.x seam: a `wait`-enter failure leaves `inflight` set (drop the flow); full-duplex + multi-op pipelining (payload-region partitioning). Proven in-guest by `net-echo`'s `weft_async_e2e` (`net-echo: weft-6c async E2E PASS` -- a bidirectional zero-copy round-trip over the resident `lo`: push verified server-side, pop verified out of `rx_buf`, the readiness seq advancing, single-in-flight enforced). 965/965 + boot OK + 0 EXT + spec gate (weft + weft_readiness + loom clean). As-built `docs/reference/125-weft.md` "The native `WeftFlow` push/pop/wait API".** **Weft-7 (the arc CLOSE) audit + bench LANDED:** the focused Opus-4.8-max prosecutor (the dedicated reviewer agent, model-overridden to opus per [[feedback-reviewer-model]]; MODEL start==end, no Fable fallback) + a concurrent self-audit over the WHOLE 6a-6c EL0 surface CLOSED **0 P0 / 0 P1 / 1 P2 / 3 P3, NOT dirty**. **F1 [P2]: ungated `SYS_WEFT_SHARE` -> an unprivileged Proc loops `SYS_BURROW_ATTACH`+`SYS_WEFT_SHARE` to squat the fixed `WEFT_MAX_SHARES=64` `share_id` registry (its id is never claimable -- only netd's Rweft hands the kernel an id) -> netd's `weft_ensure` starves (register returns 0) -> every flow degrades to byte-copy SYSTEM-WIDE (a cross-Proc availability DoS; no UAF/corruption/leak -> P2) -> FIXED: gate `SYS_WEFT_SHARE` on `CAP_HW_CREATE` (the driver tier netd holds, the same gate `SYS_MMIO/IRQ/DMA/PCI_CREATE` use; regression `weft.share_cap_gate` fails on pre-fix).** F2 [P3] a transient `SYS_WEFT_MAP` OOM permanently pins one flow byte-copy (the consumed-but-unmapped id re-returned idempotently -> unclaimable) + self-F1 minted-but-unclaimed leak (bounded at the 64-slot registry, netd-death-GC'd) -> per-flow `SYS_WEFT_UNSHARE` v1.x seam (#289); F3 [P3] `dev9p_close`'s `p->weft` clear -> `__ATOMIC_RELEASE` (paired with the ACQUIRE readers; sound-today-via-last-ref-excludes-readers); F4 [P3] the netd raw-pointer slice sites' netd-single-threadedness made explicit (a per-user-netd lift must add a per-slot guard). The SOUND set (the cross-Proc #847 dual-refcount ledger, share_id consume-once + unforgeability, I-30 submit-time pin / ring-TOCTOU, I-29 count clamp, I-9 RX-defer + readiness seq-cst mirror, W^X, kernel-owned geometry) all traced + survived; spec gate GREEN (`weft.tla` 1412 + liveness + the 4 buggy cfgs; `weft_readiness.tla` + buggy_lost_wake; `loom.tla`). **The throughput bench (NET-THROUGHPUT s7/s8; #269 M6) -- CORRECTED 2026-06-21 (#290; an earlier claim here that "weft is ~10x slower ... pays per-op Loom+Tweftio overhead" was WRONG):** `netperf` MW mode (the M2 twin over `WeftFlow`), run HEAD-TO-HEAD with M2 at the SAME 256 KiB, instrumented to split data-move us from POLLOUT-readiness-stall us. Ground truth: (1) weft is NOT slower -- the aggregate is a dead heat (MW 2394 vs M2 2382 KiB/s); the earlier "~4.3x slower" was a pure SIZE artifact (M2 had been at 32 KiB, too small to ever fill the 4 KiB window + never stalled, vs MW at 256 KiB which did). (2) Weft's DATA-MOVE is ~2x faster (it moves the bytes in ~half the ops -- each push absorbs more than the window since the ring >> the window; per-op cost is EQUAL, so there is NO Loom/Tweftio penalty). (3) ~95% of BOTH aggregates is the POLLOUT readiness-stall (M2 100620 us, MW 101519 us -- identical, transport-INDEPENDENT): a bulk sender fills the 4 KiB window then waits for the writable edge via the dev9p.poll bridge -- the registered seam #221 (prompt-readiness-wake) / #288 (grow the window), NOT a weft cost. The bench output + comments were rewritten to the honest data-move-vs-readiness-stall breakdown (`weft_breakdown` for both M2+MW). 966/966 (+`weft.share_cap_gate`) + boot OK + 0 EXT + the SMP gate (default+UBSan x smp4/smp8 N>=10, 0 corruption). **THE WEFT ARC (#266) IS COMPLETE** -> next is REVENANT (#231, ASK first). Closed list: `memory/audit_weft_closed_list.md`; as-built `docs/reference/125-weft.md` "The Weft-7 focused audit close + the throughput benchmark".** |
| MMU user-PTE clear + TLBI | `arch/arm64/mmu.c::mmu_uninstall_user_pte / mmu_uninstall_user_range`, `kernel/burrow.c::burrow_unmap` (call site) | P6 hardening #2 / audit F1 fix: symmetric counterpart to `mmu_install_user_pte`. Walks L0..L3, clears the leaf PTE, broadcasts `tlbi vaae1is + dsb ish + isb` for the inner-shareable domain. Called from `burrow_unmap` BEFORE the underlying pages are freed back to the buddy. Without it, stale PTEs + TLB entries persist after `SYS_BURROW_DETACH` -> content-sensitive silent corruption when buddy LIFO returns a different PA on re-attach (suspected AEGIS-256 / mallocng root cause). Invariants: idempotent on already-cleared PTEs and on never-faulted-in pages; `pgtable_root == 0` rejected with -1 (early-boot helper paths); VA bounds match `mmu_install_user_pte`'s (`vaddr >> 47 != 0` reject). Per-page cost dominated by `dsb ish` wait (microseconds); batched-TLBI optimization deferred. **No new spec** — prose validation in this row + the audit (see `memory/audit_p6_memory_model_hazards.md` F1) + the runtime test suite (599/599 PASS at landing). |
| Errno ABI surface + `snare:*` fault-note family | `kernel/include/thylacine/errno.h` (T_E_* registry; ABI-pinned by `_Static_assert`s to POSIX errno values), `kernel/include/thylacine/notes.h` (NOTE_NAME_SNARE_* family), `docs/ERRORS.md` (binding design + rollout) | P6 hardening #3a scripture (user-authorized 2026-05-26). Two coordinated registries: (a) Thylacine-wide errno header pins POSIX-aligned values (`T_E_INVAL == 22 == EINVAL`, etc.) so the pouch boundary-line patch's `[-4095,-2]->errno` passthrough works without translation; (b) `snare:*` thematic note-name family (`snare:segv`/`snare:bus`/`snare:align`/`snare:bti`/`snare:brk`/`snare:ill`/`snare:fpe`) for kernel-synthetic posts on EL0 unhandled fault, replacing the v1.0 FAULT_UNHANDLED_USER kernel extinction with per-Proc termination via `proc_fault_terminate`. **ABI commitments**: errno values are append-only; `snare:` prefix is reserved for kernel-synthetic posters (userspace SYS_POSTNOTE with a `snare:`-prefixed name MUST be rejected at `notes_post`). Adding/removing/renumbering any errno value or `snare:*` name is audit-bearing -- re-validate every syscall surface that emits the changed code + every fault-classification site. **No new spec** per the 2026-05-23 spec-to-code broadening -- prose validation in `docs/ERRORS.md` + per-header `_Static_assert`s + the audit + the runtime test suite. Rollout staged: scripture LANDED first (no code); #3a impl uses the new constants; v1.x extends to the structured 64-bit exit_status + per-touch syscall errno upgrade. **APPEND (Menagerie build-arc step 4, 2026-06-15): `T_E_NODEV = 19` (POSIX ENODEV; the MENAGERIE §10 `T_E_DEVGONE`-class)** -- the Loom device-gone terminal CQE, executing the user-ratified MENAGERIE §10 scripture (the `T_E_CANCELED = 125` Loom-5 precedent: a Loom sub-chunk appends a POSIX-fixed errno under the adopted Loom scripture). Emitted ONLY by the async (Loom) 9P-completion path (`kernel/9p_client.c::client_mark_dead_locked(c, devgone)` -> `-P9_E_NODEV` CQE; the sync front-end + boot path keep `-P9_E_IO`). Validated by `specs/loom_devgone.tla` + I-29 (the device-gone extension) + the `9p_client.async_{peer_gone,mark_devgone}_posts_nodev_cqe` tests. |
| Memory-model defense-in-depth (F3 + F4 + F5) | `mm/phys.c::phys_init` (RAM cap), `mm/phys.c::alloc_pages` (KP_ZERO barrier), `arch/arm64/mmu.c::clear_page_then_free` + `l3_walk_and_free` / `l2_walk_and_free` / `l1_walk_and_free` / `proc_pgtable_destroy`, `kernel/proc.c::proc_free` (asid_free / pgtable_destroy ordering) | P6 hardening #2 follow-up: closes the P2/P3 findings the Opus auditor surfaced alongside the F1 P1 fix. **F3** (P2) caps the buddy zone at `mem_base + 8 GiB` so `alloc_pages` never hands out a PA the kernel direct map (`l1_directmap[1..8]`) cannot reach -- otherwise the KP_ZERO loop dereferences `pa_to_kva(pa)` past the direct-map cliff and takes an unhandled EL1 translation fault. A uart diagnostic fires only when DTB-reported RAM exceeds the cap (QEMU `-m 2048` default is dormant). To raise the cap, extend `l1_directmap` first. **F4** (P2) zeroes every Proc-pgtable page (L0/L1/L2/L3) before returning it to the buddy free-list, removing the speculative-prefetch info-leak vector of L3-leaf PA-of-user-page bit-patterns surviving into recycled buddy pages; and reverses `proc_free`'s ordering so `asid_free` (inner-shareable TLB flush) runs before `proc_pgtable_destroy`, narrowing the window in which a sibling-CPU speculative walker (carrying stale ASID TLB hints) could reach a recently-recycled sub-table page. Both orderings are correct -- the F4 order is the defense-in-depth choice. **F5** (P3) adds `dsb ish` after the KP_ZERO clearing loop so a second CPU mapping the same PA via a different VA sees zeroes (single-CPU v1.0 dormant; Phase 5+ SMP load-bearing). **No new spec** per the 2026-05-23 spec-to-code broadening -- prose validation in this row + the audit (`memory/audit_p6_memory_model_hazards.md` F3 + F4 + F5) + the runtime test suite (599/599 PASS at landing, default + UBSan). |
| 9P client (pipeline restoration, #841) | `kernel/9p_client.c`, `kernel/9p_session.c`, `kernel/9p_transport.c`, `kernel/9p_attach.c`, SrvConn transport boundary (`kernel/srvconn.c` client send/recv + `kernel/9p_srvconn_transport.c`) | Wire protocol, fid lifecycle (I-11), tag uniqueness (I-10), no-lost-wakeup (I-9 per-rpc rendez), flow control, out-of-order completion. **#841 restores committed ARCH §21/§21.10 pipelining (elected-reader, Plan 9 `mountio`) from the R15-c F230 serial regression** -- the single per-client spinlock held ACROSS the blocking `recv` + the 30s per-op deadline that desynced the shared 9P byte stream (root cause of the stalk-3c-d "UBSan flake": corvus's post-pivot X-search `Tgetattr` over the joey-shared Stratum client busy-spins a CPU stratumd needs -> 30s `TSLEEP_TIMEDOUT` -> stream desync + transport ERROR-latch -> corvus exits -> kproc `wait_pid` wrong-pid extinction). As-built: lock NEVER held across `recv`; multi-in-flight tag-demux; per-rpc reply buffer; no per-op timeout (block until reply or ring-EOF; death-interruptible via #811). Public `p9_client_*` API unchanged (dev9p + consumers untouched). **No new spec** per the 2026-05-23 broadening -- but `specs/9p_client.tla` (clean + the 4 buggy cfgs: tag_collision / ooo_match / fid_after_clunk / unbounded) is the pre-commit gate; prose validation in ARCH §21.10 + this row + the audit + the multi-in-flight runtime tests + the #841 UBSan/`forkstorm`/`capbare` repro GREEN across N boots under host load. Preempts the stalk-3c-d close. **As-built close**: the boot-hang root cause was a SEPARATE latent bug the removed 30s deadline had masked -- `kernel/devsrv.c::devsrv_close` honored `kernel_attached` on the SERVER endpoint, suppressing the ring EOF that wakes the no-timeout client (corvus's post-BadFormat Q11 teardown -> joey's Tclunk hung forever); FIXED by skipping teardown ONLY for the kernel-attached CLIENT endpoint (`(c->flag & CSRVCLIENT) && kernel_attached`) -- the SERVER endpoint always tears down (regression `devsrv.kernel_attached_server_close_eofs`, non-vacuous). Focused audit closed 1P1+1P2+3P3: F1[P1] reply-buffer UAF (read/readdir/readlink alias the per-op buffer `client_run` freed before the caller copies out) FIXED via `c->done_reply_buf` deferred-free; F2[P2] DIED-leaked outstanding slot **CLOSED by #845 (Tflush-on-abandon, see the addendum at the end of this row)**; F3/F5 reconciled in §21.10 (send is all-or-nothing-fail not block-on-room; demux-malformation also deaths the session); F4 accepted. Verified: default 704/704 + UBSan 3/3 + smp8 2/2 + capbare 12/12 under load + spec gate (clean + 4 buggy cfgs). **DIRTY-CLOSE RECURSION (the restructure changed a wait/wake protocol): round-2 prosecuted the death/hand-off SMP path round-1 only reasoned about + found F6[P1] (reader-role-loss strands a survivor when a hand-off target's Proc dies before assuming the role -> re-hand-off on the DIED path, be_reader-gated) + F7[P2] (be_reader never cleared on election-race-loss -> busy-spin -> clear before sleeping) + F8[P3] (destroy free now under c->lock), all FIXED; round-3 prosecuted the round-2 fixes + hand-off completeness -> CLEAN 0/0/0/0. CONVERGED clean over 3 rounds. Closed list: `memory/audit_841_closed_list.md`. Owed: a deterministic multi-in-flight/cross-Proc-death unit test (the SMP window the synchronous harness can't produce) -- lands with the A-5b multi-user workload. **#845 Tflush-on-abandon addendum** (`c31e7fd` + close): closes the F2 DIED-leaked slot via 9P Tflush -- the protocol's request-cancellation (Plan 9 mount driver + Linux v9fs). On CLIENT_WAIT_DIED the client sends `Tflush(oldtag=T)` under `c->lock`; T stays reserved (`outstanding[].awaiting_flush`) and is freed ONLY by its `Rflush`, NEVER by a late original reply (the I-10 reuse-race guard -- per 9P oldtag is not reusable until Rflush, so no stray/duplicate reply is mis-attributed to a reused tag). The flush is ownerless (no `inflight[F]`); a survivor's elected reader drains the Rflush via `demux_frame_locked`'s ownerless dispatch (`p9_session_dispatch_rmsg` routes the late-original = consume-without-clear, AND the Rflush = TFLUSH branch frees oldtag + the tail frees the flush tag). Fallback to the pre-#845 path if the flush can't be built/sent (no regression); a failed transport write latches the session dead. New wire `p9_build_tflush`/`p9_parse_rflush`; `struct p9_outstanding += awaiting_flush + flush_oldtag`. stratumd already Rflushes (lp9 + p9 servers) -> Thylacine-only. Audit (Opus R1) **0 P0 + 0 P1 + 1 P2 + 3 P3**: F1[P2] dup-Rflush-on-a-REUSED-flush-tag = the generic "server sends <=1 reply per tag" wire trust assumption (no per-tag wire generation in 9P; v1.0-UNREACHABLE with trusted stratumd/dev9p; the existing `awaiting_flush` guard is already maximal) -> CLOSED-with-justification + v1.x untrusted-server seam; F2[P3] test-strengthen (end-to-end reclaim-then-reuse) FIXED; F3[P3] late-Rwalk-skips-fid_bind divergence DOC; F4[P3] dead `out->kind` FIXED. Tests 704->707 (`9p_wire.tflush_round_trip`, `9p_session.flush_reclaims_both`, `9p_session.late_reply_does_not_free_awaiting_flush`). Matrix: default smp4 + smp8 + UBSan 707/707 + 0 EXTINCTION + login E2E + spec gate (clean + 4 buggy cfgs). Owed (shared with #841): the deterministic multi-in-flight harness exercising the live DIED->Tflush->survivor-reader path -- lands with A-5b. Closed list: `memory/audit_845_closed_list.md`. **#349 send-side flow control addendum** (the on-device `go build` blocker's masking layer): a transiently-FULL c2s ring is BACK-PRESSURE, not session death. Pre-#349 `srvconn_client_send_frame`'s 0 ("ring full but ALIVE") collapsed to -1 and `client_run` marked the WHOLE shared dev9p session dead -- killing every in-flight op incl. a PEER's in-flight REVENANT text page-in (Twrite back-pressure -> `snare:bus` + an `-EIO` cascade across the joey-shared Stratum client). FIX: a `P9_TRANSPORT_EAGAIN` (-11) sentinel threaded `srvconn_transport_send` (n==0) -> `do_send` (propagated ONLY at sent==0; mid-frame EAGAIN stays fatal) -> `client_send_flow` (replaces the raw send in `client_run`): on EAGAIN, self-pump one s2c frame when no reader (drain -> server frees c2s; the deadlock-breaker) else PARK until a reader bumps `send_progress` / the session dies, then RETRY. The op's own tag is NOT on the wire (all-or-nothing send), so a self-pump only demuxes OTHER ops' replies. **MULTI-WAITER (R2-F1, the audit's headline)**: the client is shared across every Proc whose territory resolves through its mount, so N senders can be back-pressured at once -- a single `Rendez` is single-waiter (extincts on the 2nd sleeper, an unprivileged SMP-reachable PANIC on exactly the parallel-`go build` workload), so senders park on a `poll_waiter_list send_waiters_list` (each on its OWN stack `Rendez` via a `poll_waiter`; `client_send_progress_signal`/SA-1 wake them ALL; lock order c->lock -> list -> rendez; the audited poll.tla register-then-observe). SA-1: `client_mark_dead_locked` (the SOLE c->dead setter) wakes the list so no parked sender strands on a death. The 2 Tflush sends + the async `submit_async` keep their existing fail-close (#845 flush-fallback / the pre-existing #350 seam); `client_run` is the only EAGAIN-aware caller. **No new spec** (`9p_client.tla` models tag/fid/ooo, not flow control -- unchanged + re-gated). Tests: `9p_client.send_backpressure_self_pump` (PROVEN non-vacuous: pre-fix 1005/1006 FAIL, post-fix PASS) + `9p_client.send_backpressure_multi_waiter` (the F1 structural guard: 2 waiters coexist + both wake, no extinction). The `eagain_budget` knob added to `kernel/9p_transport_mq.c`. **Audit CONVERGED CLEAN over 2 rounds (Opus-4.8-max + concurrent self-audit each; MODEL(end)=claude-opus-4-8 both)**: R1 0 P0 / **1 P1** / 1 P2 / 1 P3 -> DIRTY (the self-audit MISSED F1, the formal round caught it -- the exact value of running both): F1[P1] the single-waiter `send_rendez` extinction (FIXED -> multi-waiter `poll_waiter_list`); F2[P2] the test covered only the self-pump branch (FIXED -> the multi_waiter test); F3[P3] self-pump recv-error latches-dead (sound, doc'd). R2 on the multi-waiter restructure CONVERGED CLEAN 0/0/0/1 (the P3 = the multi_waiter test proves the mechanism but not the live park `sleep()` loop -- the owed deterministic two-thread-same-client harness, shared with #841/#845/Loom). Verified: default+UBSan 1007/1007 + the SMP gate (default+UBSan x smp4/smp8 N=10, 0 corruption) + the doc-per-PR (`docs/reference/47-9p-client.md` "Send-side flow control"). Closed list: `memory/audit_349_closed_list.md`. v1.x SEAM: #350 (the async `submit_async` EAGAIN-as-fatal -- same class, pre-existing, the clean fix needs the async on_complete-double-fire design). |

| `AT_HWCAP` exec-auxv CPU-feature word (the CF-4 A AEAD lever) | `arch/arm64/hwfeat.{c,h}` (`g_hw_features.linux_hwcap` — the Linux-uapi-numbered word derived from ID_AA64ISAR0_EL1 + ID_AA64PFR0_EL1 at `hw_features_detect`: FP/ASIMD [PFR0 inverted-sentinel fields] + AES/PMULL/SHA1/SHA2/SHA512/SHA3/CRC32/ATOMICS/ASIMDDP), `kernel/include/thylacine/elf.h` (`AT_HWCAP = 16` — the STANDARD SysV tag, unlike the deliberately-private `AT_VDSO_CLOCK`), `kernel/exec.c::exec_fill_auxv` (+1 unconditional entry; both frame shapes route through it), `kernel/include/thylacine/exec.h` (`EXEC_INIT_AUXV_COUNT` 7 -> 8; Shape-A frame 160 -> 176); consumers: pouch libsodium (`tools/build.sh` compiles the self-arming armcrypto TUs, runtime-gated on `getauxval(AT_HWCAP) & (1<<3)`), the Go fork (`os_thylacine.go` sysargs -> `internal/cpu.HWCap` + `cpu_arm64_thylacine.go`) | The CF-4 A AEAD lever (CONCURRENT-FS.md; measured: the go-build cold window was 20.0 s of 20.7 s inside SOFT AEGIS-256 decrypt while the CPU's AES extensions idled behind the missing feature word). **An exec-ABI addition — audit-noted, not privilege-bearing**: the word is read-only boot-derived info (I-15: derived from ID regs, like the banner), leaks no secret/layout (no KASLR interaction), and is APPEND-ONLY (a consumer treats unknown-clear as absent). Invariants: the bits must be TRUTHFUL (a set bit whose instructions extinct on this CPU = a SIGILL time bomb in every consumer; a clear bit = silent soft fallback — fail-safe by construction on crypto-less cores, RPi4's A72); **`hwcap_CPUID` (bit 11) must NEVER be set** while Thylacine lacks Linux's EL0 MIDR trap-and-emulate (Go's `hwcapInit` calls `getMIDR()` — an EL0 `mrs midr_el1` — when it sees CPUID; on Thylacine that is `snare:ill`); auxv consumers scan by tag to AT_NULL (verified: musl, libthyla-rs, the Go fork — no fixed-offset parser exists), so the +1 entry is layout-safe. RECORDED SEAM (audit F5): the word is BOOT-CPU-derived (before smp_init); a heterogeneous target must AND-in secondary ID regs at smp_init before the first exec (the Linux sanitized-view analog) — all current targets are homogeneous and the W1.5 LSE patcher carries the identical assumption. Proof: the `exec.setup_auxv` kernel tests (tag order + the FP\|ASIMD floor + the hwcap value) + the pouch-hello-sodium AGREEMENT probe (`sodium_runtime_has_armcrypto()` must equal the AT_HWCAP AES bit — proves the hardware path live on AES CPUs AND the fail-safe on AES-less ones, boot-fatal) + the bench re-measure. **No new §28 invariant; no new spec** per the 2026-05-23 broadening — prose in CONCURRENT-FS.md CF-4 A + this row + the focused audit + the SMP gate. |

The FULL prosecution list is the ARCH §25.4 row (the authoritative copy).** Prosecute: W^X (lazy fault installs RW/XN, never executable); charge-on-fault correctness + graceful-OOM (over-`PROC_PAGE_MAX` commit fails the fault -> `proc_fault_terminate`, never a box extinction; no torn count / underflow; `page_count` == true RSS); the SMP install-once race (two CPUs fault one slot -> loser frees; the REVENANT FILE-arm class but no blocking read -> fully under `vma_lock`, no slow path); decommit lifetime (TLBI **before** free-to-buddy; idempotent on an unfaulted slot; valid only on ANON_LAZY); the `PROC_VMA_MAX` DoS bound (the free lazy reservation cannot exhaust the vma slab; eager is a no-op); lock order (`vma_lock -> v->lock`); the eager path byte-unchanged (exec data / DMA / Weft rings keep `burrow_create_anon`). **No new TLA+ spec** (prose + audit, exactly as the near-identical REVENANT `BURROW_TYPE_FILE` arm) — prose in ARCH §6.5 + §28 I-32 + `docs/reference/NN-overcommit.md` (with the impl) + this row + the focused audit + the kernel tests + the **Go stock-`heapAddrBits=48` proof** (a 512-MiB page-summary reserve commits nothing until touched) + the SMP gate. |
| `torpor_wait` / `torpor_wake` | `kernel/torpor.c`, `kernel/syscall.c` handlers, `arch/arm64/uaccess.S` (new `uaccess_load_u32`) | Wait-on-address — no-lost-wakeup (I-9 specialized; register-then-observe under `torpor_lock`), stack-waiter lifetime, uaccess fault routing. **No `specs/futex.tla`** per the 2026-05-23 spec-to-code broadening — prose validation in `torpor.h` + this audit-trigger row is the rigor. **Go-arc lock-free pre-lock compare (the osyield floor)**: after the R-5-F1 pre-fault load, a `prefault != expected` mismatch returns `TORPOR_OK` WITHOUT taking `torpor_lock` (the Linux-futex compare-before-queue shape) — sound because no waiter is registered on that path (I-9's window exists only between register and sleep, reached only by the equal path); the mismatch return deliberately provides only the plain aligned-u32 load's ordering (single-copy-atomic), not the old incidental acquire-over-`torpor_lock` — every consumer (musl `__futexwait` loops, Go `futexsleep` re-checks, libthyla-rs `torpor::wait`'s documented re-check contract) orders its own data, the universal futex contract. Removes the global-lock acquire from 36.8M of a go build's 67.7M `torpor_wait` calls (all on one `sleepDummy` bucket — sharding could never help). | pouch AF_INET socket-compat boundary-line (net-5) | `usr/lib/pouch/patches/0016-pouch-net-sockets.patch` (the 11-file musl stacking patch, on 0006), `usr/pouch-hello/pouch-hello-net.c` (the prover), `usr/pouch-hello/pouch-hello-sockets.c` (subtest-A AF_INET6 update), `usr/joey/joey.c` (the net-5 PROBE), `tools/build.sh` (wiring) | net-5 (NET-DESIGN §7; closes W4-F2). Composes the SAME I-1/I-5/I-23/I-28, adds NO new invariant; a buggy `net` client corrupts only its own state (the kernel + netd validate). Loom composition: a Loom READ on `data` composes with net-6a-1 `poll_data` (recv stream), a Loom LOPEN on `listen` composes with net-3a `PendingAccept` (async accept). **Seams -> net-8** (which owns the in-guest peer): the live cross-Proc native-API round-trip (netd's live stack is NIC-only -> no loopback route), the literal §12.1 multishot-*read*-on-`listen` accept loop (wants a netd listen-read-defer; net-3a defers the *open*), and a backlog > 1. Self-audit clean (`File` Drop closes ctl+data; parse/read bounds checked; `echo_e2e`'s slot-free balance mirrors the audited `lo_tcp_accept`). **No new spec**; prose in NEW `docs/reference/122-net.md` + NET-DESIGN §20 + this addendum + the `/net-echo` + `netd: net-6a-3 echo E2E PASS` probes + 930/930 + boot OK + the SMP gate. The formal net-6 audit is net-6b. **net-6b-3 ADDENDUM (the pouch `poll()`/`select()` readiness translation; NEW `usr/lib/pouch/patches/0018-pouch-net-poll.patch` stacking on 0017/0016/0015, + the `pouch-hello-net.c` poll control surface; PURE userspace, kernel BYTE-UNCHANGED):** makes pouch/Linux `poll()`/`select()`/`pselect`/`ppoll` work over an AF_INET `/net` socket. The hazard: a tagged socket fd's `kernel_fd` is the `/net/<proto>/N/data` fd -- a REGULAR dev9p file, which the kernel `dev9p.poll` slot (net-6b-2b) treats as POSIX always-ready (it probes only a `QTPOLL`-marked Spoor), so the 0015 tag-dispatch (which polls `kernel_fd`) reports a `/net` socket ready unconditionally (a `poll(POLLIN)` returns instantly; `select()` reports every `/net` fd ready always). FIX: a new slot helper `pouch_sock_poll_fd` resolves the POLL TARGET (distinct from `pouch_sock_kernel_fd`, the I/O target) -- a FAM_INET socket polls its `/net/<proto>/N/ready` sibling (the `QTPOLL` readiness file, lazily opened on first poll + held for the socket's lifetime, closed at `close()` alongside `ctl_fd`), a FAM_UNIX socket keeps polling its `/srv`-stream `kernel_fd` (unchanged); the events bits pass straight through (the kernel threads them as the readiness `Tread` offset; POLLIN=0x001/POLLOUT=0x004 align across pouch/kernel/netd). `src/select/poll.c` routes its tagged-fd dispatch through `pouch_sock_poll_fd`; `select`/`pselect`/`ppoll` inherit (they route through `poll()` per 0005). NO new kernel surface (only a `SYS_open` of the readiness file). Composes the SAME I-1/I-5/I-23/I-28 + I-9 (the kernel dev9p.poll register-then-observe, `net_poll.tla`); adds NO new invariant. Prosecute (the formal net-6b audit, net-6b-4): the ready-fd lifecycle (opened once, closed exactly once on every close/error path; the concurrent-same-fd-poll + the close-vs-lazy-open race reconciled under the slot lock -- the inherited single-user-per-socket discipline); the FAM_UNIX non-regression (kernel_fd path byte-equivalent); the events-passthrough correctness. **v1.0 seam -- listener-poll (#220):** netd's `check_ready` reports `can_recv()` (false for a TCP listener), so a `poll(listener, POLLIN)` does not wake on a pending accept (the `select()`-server multiplex pattern) -- the blocking accept via `open(listen)` (net-3a) is the working path; no v1.0 in-VM consumer polls a listener; candidate fix = `check_ready` reports `accept_ready` for an ANNOUNCED TCP slot (proven via a loopback E2E), weighed at net-6b-4. Self-audit clean; **No new spec**; prose in `docs/reference/78-pouch.md` (the AF_INET backend, the poll subsection) + `docs/reference/121-netd.md` (the listener-poll seam) + NET-DESIGN §12.2 (the net-6b-3 as-built) + this addendum + the `/pouch-hello-net` poll control surface (a connected UDP socket POLLOUT-ready + POLLIN-times-out, the load-bearing wait proof) + 931/931 + boot OK + the net-6b-4 SMP gate (kernel byte-unchanged). |

Invariants: the caller's offset reaches the Dev verbatim (wire-asserted via the dev9p loopback Tread/Twrite offset capture) and the cursor is NEVER read or advanced on any path; `off < 0` + `off+len > INT64_MAX` (u64 arithmetic, no UB) + `!dev->seekable` (the POSIX ESPIPE shape — pread on a pipe fails up front, BEFORE the len==0 short-circuit, never silently a cursor-free stream op) all reject; the #844 ref-held lookup + #81 CWALKONLY reject (len 0 included) + the #3 errno clamp carry over byte-identically (the cursor arms of the shared inners are byte-identical to the pre-#37 bodies); NO weft fast-path (a weft flow is a stream — documented, deliberate). **#47 (same chunk, the #46 sibling): SYS_WSTAT's fd gate dropped RIGHT_WRITE -> kind-gate-only** — POSIX fchmod/fchown work on an O_RDONLY fd (omode-derived RIGHT_READ-only handle, A-3 F1); the write AUTHORITY is `perm_wstat_check` (the identity axis: owner-or-CAP), which is unchanged and now the ONLY write-authority gate on that path — do not weaken it; the #46 endowed-fd exception carries over (rights bound byte I/O + transfer, never the identity axis). Invariants: SYS_FSTAT kind gate (KOBJ_SPOOR, ANY rights, rejects KOBJ_SRV — #46 dropped the original RIGHT_READ tightening: POSIX fstat(2) works on any valid fd [Linux O_WRONLY/O_PATH; Plan 9 Tstat / 9P2000.L Tgetattr have no open/read requirement], an O_WRONLY create mints a WRITE-only handle per A-3 F1 and cmd/go's putIndexEntry fstats exactly such an fd for its truncate no-op gate [the -1 self-deleted every fresh go-cache index entry, #36 layer 4]; the tightening guarded nothing since metadata is reachable via an O_PATH re-walk per #81; follows the SYS_LSEEK rights-0 precedent; in-guest regression = joey `probe46`, boot-fatal, quiet + post-build-churned pool); struct t_stat layout pinned by `_Static_assert`s on every field offset (so a future kernel field add cannot land without bumping the ABI assertions); SYS_LSEEK overflow check on SEEK_CUR/SEEK_END (INT64_MAX/MIN bounds); SYS_LSEEK rejects new_offset < 0 (POSIX EINVAL); kernel partial-walk reject (`w->nqid != nname`) closes the missed-walk-returns-source-fd vector; devramfs walk now respects sys_walk_open's "return nc" contract (pre-fix it allocated its own spoor and walk_open silently failed). Pouch-side: open() → openat() forwarding closes the SYS_open=0xFFFF bypass; fstat() translates t_stat → musl's struct stat field-by-field. **No new spec** per the 2026-05-23 spec-to-code broadening — prose validation in `docs/reference/87-pouch-fstat-lseek.md` + this row + the audit + joey's `/system.key` probe (walk + fstat + lseek SEEK_END/SEEK_SET round-trip; runs on every boot). |
| pouch abort -> _Exit override | `usr/lib/pouch/patches/0011-pouch-abort.patch` (overrides musl's `src/exit/abort.c` to `_Exit(127)` directly), `usr/joey/joey.c` (retry+drain+reap workaround that depends on the override for clean stratumd exit semantics) | P6-pouch-stratumd-boot sub-chunk 16b-γ-mount-close — the documented v1.x extension landed early because the bdev read-I/O fix unblocks downstream stratumd mount code paths that exercise `assert()` / `abort()`. Upstream musl's `abort()` reaches `a_crash()` (a deliberate NULL deref) as a last-resort kill; at v1.0 the kernel's FAULT_UNHANDLED_USER policy extincts the entire boot rather than terminating the offending Proc. Invariants: WIFEXITED + WEXITSTATUS == 127 replaces Linux's WIFSIGNALED + WTERMSIG == SIGABRT (behavioral delta documented in the patch header + `docs/reference/83-pouch-signals.md`); no raise(SIGABRT) means SIGABRT handlers do NOT see the synthesized note (the override is incompatible with programs that need to run cleanup in a SIGABRT handler — those need v1.x sigaction expansion); `_Exit(127)` is async-signal-safe (the only contract it must hold). **Multi-thread hazard** (audit-bearing v1.x lift per `audit_p6_pouch_stratumd_boot_16b_gamma_mount_close_closed_list.md::F1`): `_Exit` routes through `__NR_exit_group` → kernel `SYS_EXITS`, which extincts the kernel if the Proc has live peer threads. Safe-use envelope: abort() reachable only pre-thread-spawn OR post-thread-join. The fix is SYS_EXIT_GROUP -- now DESIGNED (scripture-first: ARCH §7.9.1 + invariant I-24; task #809, in progress): a new kernel syscall that cascades peer-thread termination + the cross-thread shootdown (flag-and-self-terminate at the EL0-return checkpoint; also closes the documented `kill -> -EIO in multi-thread Proc` from 13b R1-F9). Until the impl lands, the safe-use envelope above holds. Hard prerequisite for 16c (satisfied). **No new spec** per the 2026-05-23 spec-to-code broadening — prose validation in `docs/reference/86-pouch-stratumd-boot.md` 16b-γ-mount-close section + this row + the audit. |

| 9P-srvconn transport adapter | `kernel/9p_srvconn_transport.{c,h}` (new; parallel to `kernel/9p_spoor_transport.{c,h}`); call site in `sys_attach_9p_srv_handler` | P6-pouch-stratumd-boot 16c -- the second `p9_transport_ops` backend (after `p9_spoor_transport`). Wraps a byte-mode `struct SrvConn`'s `c2s` (kernel-client -> server) + `s2c` (server -> kernel-client) byte rings into the `send` / `recv` / `close` vtable that `p9_transport_round_trip` drives. **Invariants**: the wrapped SrvConn MUST be byte-mode (`__atomic_load_n(&cn->byte_mode, ACQUIRE) == true`) -- 9P-mode SrvConns already have an embedded kernel-owned `p9_client` driving Tread/Twrite on `client_fid`, and a second `p9_client` over the same rings would race. The adapter takes a `srvconn_ref` at init and `srvconn_unref`s at close (mirrors `p9_spoor_transport`'s owns_spoors=true discipline; SrvConn refcount is the lifetime authority). The adapter's `recv` blocks on `s2c` via `srvconn_client_recv` (deadline-bounded by `srvconn_set_client_deadline`); `send` writes `c2s` via `srvconn_client_send` (non-blocking; SRVCONN_RING_CAP is sized to a full msize frame so a synchronous single-frame-in-flight client never blocks). **No new spec** per the 2026-05-23 spec-to-code broadening -- the framing + ordering invariants are inherited from `kernel/9p_session.c` + `kernel/9p_transport.c` (audited Phase 5); prose validation in the new `docs/reference/88-pouch-stratumd-boot-16c.md` + this row + the audit + a new kernel-internal test. |
| `SYS_ATTACH_9P_SRV` syscall | `kernel/syscall.c::sys_attach_9p_srv_handler` (new; parallel to `sys_attach_9p_handler`), `kernel/include/thylacine/syscall.h::SYS_ATTACH_9P_SRV` (new number), `usr/lib/libt/include/thyla/syscall.h::t_attach_9p_srv` | P6-pouch-stratumd-boot 16c -- the bridge from a client-held `KObj_Srv` connection handle to a mountable `KOBJ_SPOOR` dev9p root. Composes: SrvConn handle lookup -> byte-mode gate (-1 if 9P-mode -- the embedded `p9_client` reservation prevents double-driving the rings) -> kmalloc `p9_srvconn_transport` adapter -> `p9_attached_create` (drives Tversion + Tattach) -> `p9_attached_root_spoor` -> handle_alloc as KOBJ_SPOOR with R|W|TRANSFER. **Invariants**: rights gate (`RIGHT_READ` + `RIGHT_WRITE` on the SrvConn handle -- the kernel 9P client writes Twalk/Tread/Twrite and reads Rwalk/Rread/Rwrite); aname bounds (`SYS_ATTACH_ANAME_MAX` same as SYS_ATTACH_9P); n_uname u32 bound check; full failure-path rollback (every kmalloc + every spoor / srvconn ref taken is released on any error). Adopts the same `p9_attached_install_transport` ref-discipline as SYS_ATTACH_9P. **The byte-mode gate matters**: a 9P-mode SrvConn (which corvus mints) is reserved for the kernel-owned p9_client's Tread/Twrite stream -- SYS_ATTACH_9P_SRV rejects it because a second 9P client over the same rings would interleave frames. Pouch sockets (sub-chunk 12) post BYTE-mode via `SYS_POST_SERVICE_BYTE`, so stratumd's `/srv/stratum-fs` listener naturally produces byte-mode SrvConns. **stalk-3b-β update (`46ff378` D + the 3b-β-E close `d6724a0`):** the source endpoint moved `KObj_Srv` -> a `KOBJ_SPOOR` CSRVCLIENT conn Spoor (C1 `42ce2e0`; reached by open=connect on a byte-mode `/srv` service via `kernel/stalk.c` -> `kernel/devsrv.c::devsrv_open_connect`, NOT SYS_SRV_CONNECT). The handler lookup is now KOBJ_SPOOR + CSRVCLIENT flag + `devsrv_conn_of`; the composition is the SHARED `kernel/9p_attach.c::srvconn_attach_dev9p_root` (which also drives `devsrv_open_connect`'s 9p-mode path). The embedded per-SrvConn `p9_client` is RETIRED (D `46ff378`) -- the byte-mode gate no longer reserves "the embedded client" (there is none); it enforces a clean separation: a 9P-mode service is connected via open=connect directly (yielding a dev9p root), so attaching one is meaningless and rejected. **3b-β-E F1 (`devsrv.c`):** `srvconn_attach_dev9p_root` calls `srvconn_set_kernel_attached` once the adapter commits, and `devsrv_read`/`devsrv_write`'s CSRVCLIENT branches MUST honor it (`kernel_attached -> -1`) -- the no-direct-I/O-on-the-rings guard the KOBJ_SRV r/w arms carry, which had to FOLLOW the endpoint from KOBJ_SRV to KOBJ_SPOOR (regression test `devsrv.kernel_attached_io_refused`). **No new spec** per the 2026-05-23 spec-to-code broadening -- prose validation in `docs/reference/88-pouch-stratumd-boot-16c.md` + `docs/reference/70-devsrv.md` + `memory/audit_stalk3b_closed_list.md` + this row + the audit + kernel + integration tests. |
| `SYS_PIVOT_ROOT` syscall + `territory_pivot_root` | `kernel/syscall.c::sys_pivot_root_handler` (new), `kernel/territory.c::territory_pivot_root` (new core; companion to existing `territory_chroot`), `kernel/include/thylacine/syscall.h::SYS_PIVOT_ROOT` (new number), `usr/lib/libt/include/thyla/syscall.h::t_pivot_root` | P6-pouch-stratumd-boot 16c -- the long-running-Proc root swap that joey performs LAST in bringup to flip its territory from the bootstrap devramfs root to the disk-backed Stratum FS root. Closes the v1.x note in `usr/joey/joey.c:293-304` ("v1.x adds SYS_UNCHROOT or a proper pivot_root"). **Semantics** (mirrors Linux `pivot_root(2)` minus the put_old argument -- the displaced root is simply unreferenced): under the Proc's territory lock, `spoor_ref(new_root_spoor)` then atomically replace `territory->root_spoor` with the new ref then `spoor_clunk(old_root_spoor)`. Idempotent on same-spoor (returns 0 without bumping). **Why distinct from re-`SYS_CHROOT`**: the existing `territory_chroot` allows the displaced root's ref to drop, but it is documented as "subsequent SYS_CHROOT replaces it"; a NEW syscall + core makes the long-running-Proc usage explicit and audit-trackable, and lets the per-Proc semantics evolve (e.g., post-pivot `/sbin` bind-survivor in v1.x) without re-litigating SYS_CHROOT's contract. **Rights gate**: source fd is `KOBJ_SPOOR` with `RIGHT_READ`. **Invariants**: I-1 (the new root_spoor is a tree the caller already has read rights on -- isolation preserved); I-3 (mount DAG is per-Territory; a pivot replaces one root without introducing cycles); territory-mount-refcount consistency (the displaced root's mounts in the per-Proc mount table are NOT carried over -- mount entries are root-relative and the caller is responsible for re-establishing any binds against the new root; for joey's v1.0 usage that re-establishment is none, since pivot is the last bringup step). **No new spec** per the 2026-05-23 spec-to-code broadening -- prose validation in this row + `docs/reference/88-pouch-stratumd-boot-16c.md` + the audit + kernel + boot-path integration tests. |
| `kernel_attached` SrvConn gate (16c-integration) | `kernel/srvconn.{c,h}::srvconn_set_kernel_attached` + `srvconn_is_kernel_attached`; `struct SrvConn::kernel_attached` (new field); `kernel/handle.c::handle_release_obj` KOBJ_SRV branch; `kernel/syscall.c::sys_attach_9p_srv_handler` setter call (at end, after all failure paths); `kernel/9p_srvconn_transport.c::srvconn_transport_close` (now does srvconn_teardown + srvconn_unref) | P6-pouch-stratumd-boot 16c-integration (`457f22d`). Closes the CORVUS-DESIGN.md section 6.2 "close handle = close connection" hazard for kernel-attached SrvConns: when the kernel 9P client wraps a byte-mode SrvConn, the c2s + s2c rings are LOAD-BEARING -- a userspace t_close on the now-redundant KObj_Srv handle MUST NOT EOF the rings. Pre-fix this was the smoking-gun bug: joey's idiomatic `t_close(sd_srv_fd)` post-attach triggered `srvconn_teardown` via handle_close, EOFing c2s before the very first Twalk could land. **Mechanism**: new one-way flag on `struct SrvConn` (false -> true); atomic store-release set by `srvconn_set_kernel_attached(cn)` at the END of `sys_attach_9p_srv_handler` (after all failure paths cleared, before the syscall returns the attach_fd to userspace); atomic load-acquire read by `handle_release_obj`'s KOBJ_SRV branch. If true: SKIP `srvconn_teardown`; only `srvconn_unref`. Teardown migrates to the adapter's `transport.close` (which now does `srvconn_teardown` + `srvconn_unref`); this fires at `p9_attached_destroy` time, when the LAST KOBJ_SPOOR handle referencing the attach session drops. **Invariants**: I-9 (no wakeup is lost; the release-acquire pairing on the atomic flag ensures a cross-CPU userspace close either sees the flag set OR the syscall has not yet returned the attach_fd -- userspace cannot close a handle it has not yet received); I-2 / I-6 (rights monotonicity unaffected -- the flag adds no privilege); teardown idempotency (the non-kernel-attached path is unchanged; `srvconn_teardown` is safe-to-call-twice via the `chan_set_eof` spin_lock pattern). **Regression test**: `kernel/test/test_9p_srvconn_transport.c::kernel_attached_skips_teardown_on_handle_close` (two-part: control teardown + kernel-attached no-teardown). **No new spec** per the 2026-05-23 spec-to-code broadening -- prose validation in `srvconn.h::kernel_attached` field comment + the new test + this row + the audit. |

Equivalent in role to a Linux distro's installer copying squashfs contents onto a fresh disk, run at HOST build time instead of at runtime. Without it, joey cannot pivot to the disk-backed FS (the binaries would be unreachable post-pivot, breaking every joey spawn that resolves a `/sbin/*` or `/pouch-hello-*` path from devramfs). **The 'installer' is shell orchestration of existing Stratum v2 tools**: `stratum-mkfs` (already wired) creates the empty pool; `stratumd` is started in the background listening on a temp Unix socket; `stratum-fs write` (the audited 9P-CLI client subcommand that does `lcreate + buffered Twrite + auto-fsync`) writes each corpus file under its target path; stratumd is shut down. NOT audit-bearing on the Thylacine kernel surface (host build infra). **No new spec** -- prose validation in `docs/reference/86-pouch-stratumd-boot.md` "### The 16c live-medium + host-bake + pivot design" section + this row. |

| Kernel rwx enforcement layer (A-2d) | `kernel/syscall.c` (`perm_check` insertions: `sys_walk_open_handler` [X on src + R/W on target], `sys_walk_create_handler` [W+X on parent], `sys_wstat_handler` [chmod/chown/chgrp policy]), new `kernel/perm.c` (or fold into `kernel/proc.c`) `perm_check` + `proc_in_group`, `kernel/dev9p.c` (`dev9p_stat_native` gated on the `Rgetattr` valid mask -- closes A-2a F2) | Convergence-detour A-2d (IDENTITY-DESIGN.md sections 3.7.1 + 9.6; privilege model voted 2026-05-30). **The FIRST real exercise of I-22's enforcement obligation -- privilege boundary; prosecute hard.** Linux-VFS model (kernel enforces rwx at the FS chokepoint; Stratum enforces dataset-scope ONLY, not file rwx -- section 3.7). Invariants: owner-first POSIX algorithm (owner bits authoritative even when group/other grant more; no group/other leak when owner bits deny); group membership = `primary_gid` OR `supp_gids[0..count)` (`GID_INVALID` never a member); enforcement points = walk (X on the searched dir; per-component since walk is one-name-per-call), open (R/W per omode; `O_PATH` exempt from R/W but NOT from the path X-search), create (W+X on parent), wstat (the policy); read/write NOT re-checked (open-time snapshot); the handle RIGHT (capability axis) AND the rwx check (identity axis) are BOTH required + orthogonal. **`CAP_HOSTOWNER` is the unified v1.0 fs-admin authority** (DAC-override + chmod-any + chown-any + chgrp-any) -- a capability (elevation-only, console-gated, never rfork-able), NEVER an identity, so **no `principal_id` -- not even `PRINCIPAL_SYSTEM` -- bypasses (I-22 preserved)**; owner keeps owner|self-group chmod + chgrp-to-own-group; **no-give-away chown** (`CAP_HOSTOWNER` only). Fail-closed on a NULL `stat_native` Dev. **Honest scope**: per-principal-real on devramfs (system-owned world-r/x -> boot chain owns everything, no brick; a `CAP_SET_IDENTITY`-spawned non-system child is denied write -- testable NOW, not gated on login A-5). **dev9p enforcement DEFERRED to A-3** (user-signed-off 2026-05-30): ground truth shows uniform dev9p enforcement bricks the boot -- the host-bake stamps pool entries owned by the host uid (0644/0755), and the `PRINCIPAL_SYSTEM` boot chain (no `CAP_HOSTOWNER`) as *other* cannot write the pool, so the post-pivot creates (`/var/lib/corvus`, `susan`) would be denied. Gated by a new `Dev.perm_enforced` flag (devramfs=true, dev9p=false; the A-3 activation is a one-line flip); dev9p stays handle-RIGHT-gated only at v1.0 (no regression). The wstat ownership-change policy is also `perm_enforced`-gated -> dormant + unit-tested at v1.0, activates with dev9p at A-3. Closes A-2a audit F2. A-2b create-check folds in; A-2c mount-cape stays a seam; A-4 splits a finer `fs-admin` clearance (`CAP_DAC_OVERRIDE`+`CAP_CHOWN`) -- additive. **No new spec** per the 2026-05-23 broadening -- prose validation in IDENTITY-DESIGN.md sections 3.7.1 + 9.6 + `docs/reference/99-fs-permission.md` + this row + the audit + the runtime test suite (devramfs deny/allow via CAP_SET_IDENTITY; `perm_check`/`proc_in_group` unit tables; wstat policy paths; dev9p loopback; joey `/system.key` boot regression). |

Invariants: **C-28 no-escrow** (corvus stores no copy of a user's keypair/DEK recoverable by any authority other than that user's passphrase OR own phrase; the hostowner has NO user-data-recovery verb -> D3 mutually-encrypted-homes survives a malicious hostowner); **C-27** (per-user keyslot minted at USER_CREATE, displayed once, never persisted; same keypair as `hybrid.corvus`; domain-separated AD `"thylacine-corvus-recovery-v1"`); **C-20** generalized. Prosecute: the **gate** (RECOVER(user) = phrase + rate-limit ONLY, no session / no `CAP_HOSTOWNER`; RECOVER(system) additionally console-attached -- a token-only or non-console bypass is the bug); **phrase brute-force** (the C-16 rate-limit is the online defense; a weak-RNG / partial-checksum bug would matter); **secret hygiene** (mlock + `explicit_bzero` of phrase, recovery_KEK, keypair, new_KEK on EVERY path incl. error); the **twin-wrap atomicity** (re-wrap `hybrid.corvus` AND roll `recovery.corvus` -- a crash between must not strand the user un-recoverable nor leave the old phrase live; rename-swap, A-1.6); **no-DEK-rewrite correctness** (the recovered keypair must byte-equal the original so existing envelopes decapsulate); the **USER_CREATE OK-response growth** (callers parse the appended phrase; no overrun). **A-5c-b (host-bake) additionally**: the `corvus-crypto` extraction MUST preserve byte-identical wraps (the A-5c-a / A-1b / A-5b wrap + DEK-envelope paths are behavior-unchanged -- re-validate the boot self-test + USER_CREATE enrollment E2E); a host-minted `system-wrap` and the on-device unwrap must round-trip (same CRVS layout / AD / Argon2id preset -- no drift between `corvus-mint` and corvus); the real `handle_admin_elevate` fails CLOSED on a missing / corrupt / wrong-passphrase `system-wrap` (no byte-compare fallback survives); RECOVER(`subject_kind=0`) requires console attachment; the bake lands the files SYSTEM-owned where corvus's chroot resolves them (joey's runtime `mkdir_or_open` no-ops over the baked dir-chain). **No new spec** per the 2026-05-23 broadening -- prose validation in IDENTITY-DESIGN.md §9.9 + CORVUS-DESIGN §5.5.1/§5.6 + this row + the audit + corvus unit tests + the boot E2E (create -> capture phrase -> lose passphrase -> RECOVER -> re-login -> home decrypts; system: ADMIN_ELEVATE + RECOVER(system)). |

| Proc exit handle-close (#926) | `kernel/proc.c` (`proc_close_handles_at_exit` -- the new static helper; the top-of-`exits()` gated call `if (p->thread_count == 1) proc_close_handles_at_exit(p)` placed AFTER `srv_proc_exit_notify`/`cap_proc_exit_notify` + BEFORE the `g_proc_table_lock` acquire; the `thread_exit_self()` no-op note on the become_zombie path; the `proc_free` fallback comment), `kernel/handle.c` (`handle_table_free` lockless-safety comment -- the #844 justification updated for the new ALIVE-Proc call site) | #926 (U-6f command-substitution prerequisite; user-voted "fix the kernel" 2026-06-08). The kernel previously closed a Proc's handle table ONLY at reap (`handle_table_free` in `proc_free`, ZOMBIE-gated), so a child's inherited pipe write end stayed open in the zombie until the parent reaped it -- a shell draining `$(cmd)`'s stdout to EOF hung forever (no `write_eof`). FIX: a SINGLE-thread Proc closes its handle table at the TOP of `exits()` while still RUNNING + ALIVE + `thread_count==1` -- the only sound spot (t RUNNING so a sleep-capable close hook like a 9P clunk is legal -- sleeping while EXITING trips sched()'s "not RUNNING" assert; p ALIVE so `wait_pid` cannot reap+thread_free mid-close; `thread_count==1` so no peer shares the table). Inherited fds thus close at process termination (correct Unix/Plan 9 semantics); the parent's drain-before-reap sees EOF immediately. **Death-path surface (the #788/#806/#807/#808/#860/#809/#811 lineage) -- the most bug-prone in the tree.** Invariants: **I-7** (the #847 per-Burrow dual refcount -- free only when handle_count==0 AND mapping_count==0 -- makes the inverted handle-close-at-exit / vma-drain-at-reap ordering safe: dropping handle_count at exit while a VMA still maps does NOT free; vma_drain at reap drops the last mapping ref); no double-free (`handle_table_free(NULL)` no-ops; `proc_close_handles_at_exit` NULLs `p->handles`, so `proc_free`'s call no-ops; it remains the real close for multi-thread + the direct `state=ZOMBIE; proc_free()` orphan/rollback paths); no reaper UAF; no sleep-in-EXITING; the `thread_count==1` lockless read is stable (decrement is reap-only via `thread_unlink_from_proc`<-`thread_free`, and the sole caller-thread is not spawning). MULTI-thread Procs keep close-at-reap: their last-Thread EXITING mark is atomic-under-lock with the last-Thread determination, leaving no RUNNING window for a sleeping close -- a v1.x EXITING-protocol restructure (which also closes the killed-single-thread asymmetry: a single-thread Proc killed via `proc_group_terminate`->`thread_exit_self` defers to reap too). **SMP-gated** (default+UBSan x smp4/smp8 N=10, 0 corruption) + focused Opus audit (0 P0 / 0 P1 / 0 P2 / 3 P3, all doc: F1 the handle.c lockless justification updated, F2 the kill-path asymmetry documented, F3 `$errstr`-unchanged-on-subst-spawn-fail cosmetic). Verified by the `u-test::flow_process_pipe` part-(c) regression (drain a child's stdout to EOF BEFORE reaping -- the exact pattern formerly documented as "block forever") + the rewritten `test_sys_spawn_with_fds_child_rights_subset_of_parent` (spawns pipe-sink which BLOCKS reading fd 0, keeping it live for the rights inspection) + `/u-subst-test`. **No new spec** per the 2026-05-23 broadening -- prose in `docs/reference/14-process-model.md` + ARCH section 25.4 + this row + the audit + the regression tests. |

a DEDICATED page, nothing else on it; a user WRITE faults [`fault.c` `is_write && !VMA_PROT_WRITE` -> `FAULT_UNHANDLED_USER` -> snare:segv] so a hostile/buggy Proc can never corrupt the shared timebase), **I-15** (`freq` == CNTFRQ at `timer_init`, DTB-consistent). | The Larder: guest-side 9P FS cache (L1c substrate + attr sub-cache; L1d dentry sub-cache; L1e page sub-cache + cacheability gate) | NEW `kernel/include/thylacine/larder.{h,c}` (`struct larder` on `p9_client` -- a near-leaf lock + a bounded 256-entry LRU `qid.path`-keyed attr array + a `(parent-qid,name)`-keyed dentry array (incl. NEGATIVE) + a 512-slot `(qid.path,page_index)`-keyed page table (heap 4 KiB buffers, lazy + reused + freed at `larder_destroy`) + a monotonic invalidation `gen`; attr serve[Read]/install[Open, gen-guarded]/invalidate[OwnWrite]; dentry serve[Read]/install[Read+OwnWrite, gen-guarded]/invalidate-parent[OwnWrite]; page serve[Read, cvers-gated]/install[Open, gen-guarded]/invalidate[OwnWrite]), `kernel/9p_client.{h,c}` (embed + init `cacheable`=false + `larder_destroy` at destroy), `kernel/dev9p.c` (attr serve+populate at `dev9p_stat_native`; dentry serve + attr+dentry populate at `dev9p_walk_attrs`; page serve+populate at `dev9p_read`; attr+page invalidate at write; attr invalidate at wstat/create[parent+child]/rename/unlink; dentry-parent invalidate at create/rename[both]/unlink; **set `cacheable`=true on a successful `Twalkgetattr`**) | The Larder (`docs/LARDER-DESIGN.md`; the measured top lever of the on-device `go build`; user-voted 2026-07-09). **On the most-audited FS path (dev9p / 9p_client / stalk) -- prosecute hard; the AUTHORITATIVE prosecution list is the ARCH §25.4 row.** Realizes **I-38** (close-to-open cache coherence); NO new invariant (composes I-28/I-32/I-10/I-11). The attr serve is a `Read` (no cvers re-check -- the win); coherence = own-write invalidation + `walk_attrs` revalidate-by-overwrite -> NoWrongRead ABSOLUTE single-writer. Central obligations: serve/invalidate SMP atomicity (serve copies the t_stat out under the leaf lock; the lock is a pure leaf, never with `c->lock`/across an RPC); the **populate GEN guard** (captured pre-RPC, re-checked at install -- skips a populate that raced an invalidate, closing the populate-after-invalidate resurrection = the impl realization of the spec's atomic `Open`); the **create-reuse child-invalidate** (a reused-ino create carries a stale prior-occupant attr, and create never runs `walk_attrs` -- `dev9p_create` invalidates the child too; the `stalk-2` E2E failure, regression `dev9p.create_invalidates_reused_child`); the `qid.path`=0 root key (explicit `valid` bit); Bounded LRU (I-32); never-populate-from-readdir (L1a-2 audit-F1). **L1d dentry (the AUTHORITATIVE list is the ARCH §25.4 L1d ADDENDUM):** the dentry cache is **OWN-WRITE INVALIDATION ONLY, NOT cvers-gated** -- the L1d GROUND-TRUTH CORRECTION: Stratum surfaces no directory-content version that tracks a dirent change (verified `src/fs/fs.c` -- a child create/unlink does NOT `stm_inode_set` the parent, so the parent `si_cvers` does not bump; only rename stamps it), so a parent-cvers gate would falsely match a stale negative dentry after a create; coherence = drop the parent's dentries on `dev9p_create`/`rename`[both dirs]/`unlink`. Maps onto `fs_cache.tla`'s `Read`+`OwnWrite` subset (the attr discipline keyed by `(parent,name)`; no `Open` gate). Prosecute: the multi-hop serve atomicity (the dentry chain + each hop's attr lookup under ONE lock hold); the positive-serve attr coupling (a hop's reply attr comes from the attr cache -- an attr miss bails to the RPC); the query-only full-serve (a bind-form full walk MUST RPC to bind the fid; only the query form + any-form negative skip it); Territory-independence (raw dev9p-tree bindings; the resolver applies the mount overlay; a negative dentry can't be a mount point). **Spec-first RE-ENABLED (`specs/fs_cache.tla`, L1b)** is the pre-commit gate; **No new spec at L1c/L1d** (L1c's gen guard = prose realization of the modeled atomic Open; L1d's dentry cache is the modeled `Read`+`OwnWrite` subset -- the sketched parent-cvers gate REMOVED as unsound). Prose in `docs/LARDER-DESIGN.md` + `docs/reference/132-larder.md` + the ARCH §25.4 row + the L1f focused audit + the `larder.*`/`dev9p.*` tests + boot OK + the SMP gate. **L1e page cache + the LOAD-BEARING cacheability gate (the AUTHORITATIVE list is the ARCH §25.4 L1e ADDENDUM):** the page sub-cache keyed `(qid.path,page_index)` engages ONLY for a `cacheable` client -- a per-`p9_client` flag latched true by a successful `Twalkgetattr` (the v1.0 proxy for a content-versioned, offset-stable FS; `dev9p_walk_attrs` sets it). A stream server (netd `/net`: consuming reads, `qid.version` 0) answers `Twalkgetattr` ENOSYS -> never latches -> never cached (no stale stream bytes; also closes the latent L1c netd-attr gap). Fail-safe (default false, settled before any read; corvus is byte-mode/no-Larder; `/proc`/`/ctl`/`/env`/`/dev` are native Devs/no-Larder). Prosecute: page-buffer lifetime SMP-safety (serve COPIES out under the leaf lock; evict reuses [never frees]; invalidate/destroy free under the lock -- no free-under-copy; the `l->lock -> buddy` order, kmalloc non-blocking under the leaf lock); the cvers freshness gate (`page.cvers == c->qid.vers`, close-to-open Open; cross-open external write misses+refetches; own-writes invalidate); partial-page soundness (serve only `[0,valid_len)`, populate only from a page's aligned start -> no hole, no EOF determination -- a short RPC read could be msize-clamp not EOF); gen-guarded populate (resurrection close); whole-file over-invalidation on write (sound; per-range = v1.x); gate completeness+fail-safety (all serve/populate paths gated; the POUNCE proxy != the true property -- a future POUNCE-but-streaming server needs an explicit capability, v1.x). **NO spec extension at L1e** (a page is a content token -- the modeled `Read`+`Open`+`OwnWrite`). Tests: `larder.page_*` (10) + `dev9p.page_cache_serve_and_gate` (non-vacuous, 1076/1077 FAIL with serve disabled). 1077/1077 + boot OK + reduced SMP gate 20/20 (0 corruption). **L1f (the arc CLOSE) LANDED:** the focused Opus-4.8-max prosecutor (MODEL start==end, no fallback -- Fable out of quota) + a concurrent self-audit CLOSED **0 P0 / 1 P1 / 0 P2 / 2 P3, NOT dirty**. **F1 [P1]:** the reused-ino hazard applies to the child's PAGES exactly as to its attr -- `dev9p_create` invalidated the child attr but NOT its pages, so a create at a freed+reused `qid.path` could serve a prior occupant's stale page IF the fresh `qid.version` collides with the cached page's `cvers` (a collision the Thylacine tree cannot rule out -- it depends on Stratum's fresh-inode `si_cvers`) -> FIXED by `larder_page_invalidate(l, c->qid.path)` in `dev9p_create` (the page twin of the attr defense; data integrity must not rest on an unstated cross-project guarantee) + regression `dev9p.create_invalidates_reused_child_pages` (non-vacuous: 1077/1078 FAIL pre-fix). **F2 [P3]:** the Loom-async-mutation-bypass "unreachable" wording corrected to "not driven by any v1.0 consumer; self-inflicted-reachable" (a crafted EL0 program could self-inflict a stale view of its OWN file -- page key = qid.path, no cross-Proc/privilege leak); v1.x fix tracked. **F3 [P3, == self-audit SA-1]:** rename/unlink leave the moved/unlinked file's OWN attr -> stale `ctime`/`nlink` (metadata-only -- mode/uid/gid unchanged -> NO perm_check/I-28 impact; `nlink` moot at v1.0, hardlinks Loom-only) -> documented v1.x seam (§11). The trigger list is *cumulative*: as new audit-bearing files appear (e.g. Phase 4 adds the 9P client; Phase 5 adds futex / poll / notes / pty), they're appended here in the same PR that introduces them.

### The reviewer agent (`.claude/agents/holotype-reviewer.md`)

The prosecutor is a **dedicated agent definition**, not an inlined general-purpose subagent: `.claude/agents/holotype-reviewer.md` pins `model: fable` + `effort: max` + the standing prosecute discipline, so every round spawns it identically with only a scoped per-round prompt on top. **Run every review on Fable 5 at max effort** (re-enabled by the user 2026-07-04 after the 2026-06-13..07-04 US-Government-policy restriction; `memory/feedback_reviewer_model.md` is the single home for this decision). **Opus 4.8 at max effort is the fallback** when Fable is unavailable. The agent reports `MODEL(start)` as its first output line and `MODEL(end)` as its last, independently — both should read Fable 5; a `start != end` mismatch flags a mid-run model fallback, so weigh the affected portion and re-spawn if a key surface was reviewed after it. An on-disk agent definition loads at session START: after creating/editing the `.md`, start a fresh session (or open the `/agents` UI) before `subagent_type: holotype-reviewer` resolves — in the SAME session, pass the Agent tool's per-call `model` override instead.

### How to run an audit round

1. Spawn the dedicated reviewer agent (`subagent_type: holotype-reviewer`, `run_in_background: true`). Model + effort + the prosecute-not-defend discipline come from the agent definition; the prompt carries only the round-specific scope, invariants, and adversarial categories.
2. In the prompt, include `memory/audit_rN_closed_list.md` contents as the "already fixed — do not re-report" preamble.
3. Scope the prompt to the surface you changed.
4. Wait for the completion notification. Do not poll.
5. Trust but verify: validate quoted file:line references AND check the agent's `MODEL(start)` / `MODEL(end)` lines — a mismatch means a mid-run model fallback, so weigh the post-fallback portion accordingly (re-spawn on the stronger model if a key surface was reviewed after the fallback).
6. Fix every P0/P1/P2 finding before merge. P3 findings get tracked or closed with explicit justification.
7. Append the round's closed list to `memory/audit_rN_closed_list.md` for the cumulative do-not-re-report set.

### Prosecutor agent prompt template

```
You are an adversarial soundness prosecutor auditing {scope} against the
invariants listed in ARCHITECTURE.md §28 (the enumerated invariants).

# Scope

Commits: {SHA1}, {SHA2}, ...
Files in scope: {list}

# Invariants that MUST hold

{enumerate from ARCH §28, briefly}

# Adversarial categories to prosecute

- Privilege escalation (capability bypass, namespace escape, handle forge)
- Race conditions (wait/wake, IPI ordering, scheduler concurrency, refcount races)
- Lifetime violations (UAF, double-free, dangling Chan, dangling VMO)
- Memory safety (W^X violation, integer overflow on size paths, out-of-bounds)
- Crypto / integrity (Stratum integrity surface; janus key handling)
- Format / protocol (9P malformed messages, ELF malformed segments, DTB malformed)
- Resource exhaustion (handle table, VMO, fid pool)
- (extend per domain)

# Procedure

1. Read memory/audit_rN_closed_list.md to know the do-not-report set.
2. For each file in scope, read fully. Do NOT skim.
3. Catalog findings by severity:
   - P0: actively-broken (reproducible correctness / security / safety violation).
   - P1: latent-broken (correct today under exact test coverage, wrong under realistic deviation).
   - P2: hazard + should-land-before-merge.
   - P3: nice-to-have.
4. For each finding: file + line + prosecution chain (state → step → step → violation) + suggested fix.
5. Withdraw findings guarded by existing code. Don't re-report closed items.

Report format per finding:
## Finding F<NUM> [P<severity>]: <title>
**File**: path:line
**Invariant**: <which from §28>
**Prosecution**:
1. state that <X>.
2. attacker/crash/retry does <Y>.
3. observes <violation>.
**Suggested fix**: <1-2 sentences>

At the end: Summary with counts by severity + confidence notes on
areas you couldn't audit as deeply as you wanted. Then the final line
`MODEL(end): <model name + id>` (per your agent definition — report it
fresh; a mismatch vs MODEL(start) flags a mid-run model fallback).

Be brutal but grounded. Quote code; don't paraphrase it.
```
